< review>
I have had problems with my teeth for years. I was referred to Dr. Hakimi, and though the prognosis was bleak,  Dr. Hakimi and her staff were amazing. I have never dealt with a doctor with so much compassion.  It was very hard for me emotionally to hear what needed to be done. Dr. Hakimi and her staff explained what and why these things needed to be done. I had major work done. My recovery was painless and went exactly how I hoped it would. They have stayed in contact with me throughout, managing my progression the whole time.  I still have 4-6 months before everything is complete. I cannot wait for the final results.  Thank you Dr. Hakimi and staff for making a very difficult time much easier, and for giving me the smile I have always wanted!!!< /review>

<Name>Robert Seyfried<//Name>< rate>

< review>
Approximately 10 years ago my wife had 3 implants done to the tune of about $20,000 by Dr. Hakimi when she had her offices in Roseville.  For approximately five  (5)  years the implants were trouble free,  but this last five  years have been a nightmare for my wife, , with constant bleeding and the need for intensive daily car and my wife has done her due diligence.  Of course, Hakimi since sold her Roseville practice  and moved to Auburn, leaving all  liability  behind. Today, the first of the implants had to be removed, to the tune of $3,800  and the prognosis for the remaining two implants is poor, at best    The removal was done by Dr. Vasanthan,
who bought Hakimi's business and is now in the business of cleaning up the carnage left behind  by Hakimi.  These people are motivated  by one thing and one thing only:  PROFIT!  Good luck to you all.

I, Robert L. Seyfried, husband of Jessica Seyfried, wrote the above most critical review while in a state of both anger and disappointment, perhaps predicated upon my lack of knowledge of how this dental business works.  About 10 years ago my wife came home with a professional proposal compiled by Dr. Hakimi and another Roseville dentist whose name I can't recall.  Including the three implants the total proposal came to approximately 20K.  Gulp!  .My wife then proceeded to have all of the work performed.  I accused Dr. Hakimi of charging Jessica 20K for the implants and Dr. Hakimi rightly informed me that the implants did not cost that much, although we no longer have records of their cost.  A few years back Jessica began having some problems with the implants and she phoned Dr. Hakimi's office only to learn that Dr. Hakimi had divested herself of the Roseville practice, had moved to Auburn and that, contractually, all work done previously by Dr. Hakimi was now the responsibility of her Roseville successor, or other periodontists.  This is not the culture that I come from and my lack of understanding as respects the legalities of the dental arena made me angry.  In rebuttal to my "tirade" Dr. Hakimi's assistant informed me of the 5 years contractual  statute as respects Dr. Hakimi treating her former Roseville patients and I also learned from the same rebuttal that 5 years might be a reasonable time before implants begin to fail.  Perhaps we should have known that prior to moving forward with the procedure.  Although my wife is angry with me for venting my frustration and anger and I do apologize to Dr. Hakimi for "losing it",  I must ask where does this end?  Dr. Hakimi's successor, Dr. "Ash" charged $3,800 to remove the first implant, plus the ancillary periodontal surgery to repair the receding gum line.

I guess I just don't understand this high level  dental care and, for my ignorance,I do apologize to Dr. Hakimi for those undue critical and offensive comments I may have made.

Sincerely.

Robert Seyfried<//review>

<rate>5<//rate>< review>
I drove past on Long Beach to see a soul food place literally walking distance from my house. It being a little too warm to cook, we decided to try In The Kitchen.  Some people get upset when things are sold out, but in my book that just means, "Make an extra effort, it's that good." Missed out on Oxtail, but we had the smothered chicken and pork chops. Chicken Mac, cabbage, black eyed peas and red beans and rice were our sides.

Everything was seasoned to perfection. I could eat a bucket of that gravy alone. The cabbage was sweet and salty and the mac was outstanding and creamy. The service is fantastic. The people there are extremely kind and appreciative. The menu is small, but I rather like that since they stick to what they do best. What I do best is eat that stuff.

Welcome to the neighborhood folks. Keep making the good food and I will keep on eating it.</review>

Two years ago, got a rattle in exhaust, they replaced whole system with new muffler and cat.   Got engine code right after, they forgot to hook-up o-2 sensors, no biggy, fixed it myself.  Must add, welds on new exhaust were wonderful, I am a back-yard welder.  Here comes 2018, my jeep is telling me with code-reader that my sensor in distributor is bad, either camshaft or crankshaft, forgot, it is in distributor.   I take to my favorite place because state wants a smog check, the the heavy duty one required by state.  They oblige, I overhear owner telling his staff, "I might not make payroll next month."  He didn't know I heard him.  My Christian values sink in, tell the mechanic I have all these parts for radiator repair, why don't you put them in for me if cost is reasonable.  We agreed on price and felt good to help out shop.   I come back 2 hrs later, smog guy tells me it didn't pass, need new cat and O-2 sensors plus diagnostic. Belching Beaver is a very unique brewery. They do a lot of experimental beers here, which are all amazing! Some of the beers I sampled at the brewery were the mango IPA, peanut butter milk stout, mosaic double IPA, orange vanilla IPA and the IPA collaboration they did with the Deftones. < Review>
One of the belching beavers around Oceanside and Vista. 25% of this place is the bar and 75% is the actual brewing, packing and barrel storage. There are picnic tables, barrels to out your beer on and stand around, and a wrap around bar.

You can bring your dog, children and even play some corn hole or various other games that are behind the bar. A nice place to grab a delicious beer with friends. I enjoy all of their sour beers and the interleague ipa.

There are often food trucks available also!</Review>

<UserId.>110239633349088513540<//UserId.><username>Pradeep Mohanannair</username><time>1489723668711<//time><rating>3</rating><Review>Belching Beaver Brewery

First time to Oceanside for Beer, now I fell like I should dive in here more often, My beer town is at Miramar Area where is the melting point of micro breweries of San Diego. The ambiance is wonderful and location is very isolated and quite.

Belching Breaver beer are brewed to the Perfection. The warehouse is hard to find but its BIG, lot of space to relax and have fun.

Getting there:
Lost Abbey is really lost in San Macros, it is hard to find. Follow the directions carefully.
It's Hard to find. It is literally Lost, all the way behind few commercial buildings.

Beer Choices: Good, ~ 15 taps
*** Top 5 Beers (No-Particular Order) ***
Not my favorite places for beer, tried 4-5 beers but none was impressive.
Beavers Milk Stout: Best Basic Milk Stouts: Nice roasted flavor, very basic & no adulteration.
The Mayor - Scotch Ale W Maple, Coffee and Vanilla
OL' dirty Barrel - Bourbon Barrel aged imperial stout.
Peanut Stout
Me so Honey, decent Pale Ale

***Ambiance***
The atmosphere is like a big picnic area with lot of picnic tables and bar stools.
Lot of Fun stuffs to do, Bean bag toss, Jenga.
One small TV near the Wall Menu.

***Prices***
The prices varies on beer the range is below
Taster size: $2
Half pour size: $3-$4
Full size pour: $5-$7
Growler: $16-$20
(Growler fills are priced as 40 oz and 64 oz fills only)

***Food***
Food truck, pretty good ones.

***Try this***
Lot of Fun stuffs to do, Bean bag toss, Jenga.

***Highs***
Nice and Big setup, picnic like.
Pet Friendly

***Lows***
NOT GREAT BEERS

Hoping to come again and try different beers and update my ratings.

Big Shout out for Ritz the bartender, very friendly indeed.

**Timing**
Mon Closed
Tue Closed
Wed 4:00 pm - 8:00 pm
Thu 4:00 pm - 8:00 pm
Fri 4:00 pm - 8:00 pm
Sat 2:00 pm - 7:00 pm
Sun 1:00 pm - 6:00 pm<//Review>< pictures>

< text>
Make sure you do NOT have to use the restroom and make sure children use the restroom BEFORE you arrive. It is not the place you want to be if you need to use the restroom. Filthy at all times of the day INCLUDING opening and always poorly stocked. It's very challenging for someone with small children to make sure they "don't touch that"! Yes, it's bad enough to note in a review.

Pricing labels are poorly placed on the shelves and you REALLY have to check the SKU #s to make sure you have the correct item.  Yes, it's a toy store and of course children are going to want to play. I do sometimes too. Still, all-in-all, the store is physically a mess.

All that being said, sales associates are helpful to the point where they will search in the back and climb ladders to find items that are not on the shelf but the inventory device says there's 1 more in stock. can be a little on the shy side, they do what they can to help. I'd say 9 times our of 10 they can find it. They're usually cheerful and almost always willing to talk about their favorite toys.<//text>

< resp>
{'time': 1557100556084, 'text': 'Thanks for the review, Adam. I wish you were specific because I hear I often price my hard-to-find figures under the market price. I do have a collection of over 15,000 older comics to choose from that range from $1.50 to $1,300, but those are priced by comic condition using the Overstreet price guide and/or Ebay pricing. Most comics are less than what you can get them on Ebay, depending on the condition. I also have about 2,000 comics that are in the $1 bin. The new comics are cover price unless you get the $20/year membership, and then you get 15% off all new comics and up to 50% off the comics in the bins. For collectors, the $20 membership fee is well worth it, especially for those coming in every Wednesday to get their new comics. Comic stores can\'t really afford to sell at yard sale prices if they want to stay in business. If we don\'t make a profit, then we can\'t pay the lease, the lights, the employees, etc. This is why you often hear the phrase, "Help support your local comic book store." Many go out of business because they can\'t compete with the online businesses that don\'t have to pay for the lease, lights, employees, etc. I know we all like a "deal," which is why we offer the membership for $20 so you can feel like you\'re getting a "deal" every time you come. I think most comic book stores have some sort of membership to help keep customers loyal so it\'s not unheard of to have this at our store. Thanks again for the review.'}< /resp>

<review>This donut shop opens at 5:30am and is equipped with hot coffee, tea and a variety of freshly made donuts.
